- [x] Add YAML support to query_json (rename/extend to cover .yaml/.yml) — status: tested
  - notes: Added lib/yamlOps.js — a minimal, zero-dependency, recursive-descent YAML parser (`parseYaml`) covering block/flow mappings and sequences, quoted/unquoted scalars (strings/ints/floats/bool/null), comments, and "- key: value" inline-mapping sequence items. Explicitly rejects anchors/aliases (`&`/`*`) with a descriptive error rather than silently mishandling them (multi-doc streams, block scalars `|`/`>`, and tags are similarly out of scope by design — see file header). lib/utilOps.js gained a shared `traverseByPath()` helper (extracted from the old query_json body, also fixes a minor pre-existing bug where a JSON document whose root was literally `null` was reported as type "object" instead of "null") plus a new `queryData(filePath, query, format)` that auto-detects JSON vs YAML by extension (override via explicit `format` arg) and delegates to JSON.parse or parseYaml. `query_json` kept unchanged/untouched as a JSON-only, backward-compatible entry point. New `query_data` tool added to toolsSchema.js (schema + execute_pipeline enum) and dispatched in executeTool.js. New test/sections/05-yaml-query.js — 28 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (happy-path YAML/JSON parsing incl. flow collections and nested sequences-of-mappings, missing/empty/malformed input, anchor rejection, path traversal, shell/SQL-injection-shaped strings round-tripping as literal scalars, 50-level-deep nesting, 2000-item sequences, random fuzz bytes, a 200k-char scalar ReDoS timing check, and concurrent-read consistency). Caught and fixed one real bug during this work: a test fixture filename (`bad.json`) collided with an existing fixture of the same name in section 7's shared sandbox dir — renamed to `bad-data.json`. Full suite re-run after the fix: 118 passed, 0 failed (90 prior + 28 new). README updated: new `query_data` bullet under Utility Tools documenting the supported/unsupported YAML subset, plus `lib/yamlOps.js` row and updated `lib/utilOps.js` row in the Code Layout table.
- [x] Audit lib/processOps.js and lib/fileOps.js for security/consistency — status: tested
  - notes: Full audit pass completed. Three real issues found and fixed:
    (1) **lib/fileOps.js globToRegex `**` bug**: `c === "**"` is always false since `c` is a single character — `**` was silently treated as `*` (no cross-directory match). Fixed to `pattern.slice(i, i+2) === "**"`. This bug meant `find_files` with `**/*.js` patterns would not match across directory levels.
    (2) **lib/processOps.js ToolError upgrade**: `requireExec()` threw plain `Error`; upgraded to `ToolError(-32001)` (policy denial, consistent with executeTool's own gate). `getProcessOutput` and `killProcess` unknown-id errors upgraded to `ToolError(-32602)` (invalid params).
    (3) **lib/roots.js isWithinRoot security fix**: `resolved.startsWith(abs)` path-prefix bypass (sibling dir attack, e.g. root `/data/proj1` would incorrectly admit `/data/proj1-evil`). Fixed via `isWithinRoot(resolved, root)` helper that requires exact match OR trailing `path.sep` boundary. Fix was already in working tree (uncommitted from a previous session); committed this session.
    (4) **lib/errors.js new shared module**: `ToolError` + `getErrorCode` extracted from `executeTool.js` to `lib/errors.js` to eliminate a would-be circular dependency (`processOps` → `executeTool` → `processOps`). `executeTool.js` re-exports both for backward compatibility with `server-http.js`.
    13 new tests in test/sections/06-audit-fixes.js covering all four fixes. Full suite: 131 passed, 0 failed.
- [x] Extend yamlOps.js to support YAML block scalars (| and >) — status: tested
  - notes: Verified and completed at the start of this session (previous session was cut off mid-implementation: working tree had an uncommitted rewrite of lib/yamlOps.js plus a scratch `_smoke.js` sanity script, one local commit ahead of origin marking the task in-progress but no actual implementation commit yet). Implementation found already functionally complete on review:
    (1) **Literal (`|`) and folded (`>`) block scalars**, both as mapping values and as sequence items, with all three chomping modes — clip (default, exactly one trailing newline), strip (`-`, no trailing newline), keep (`+`, preserves trailing blank lines) — and optional explicit indentation-indicator digits (e.g. `|2`).
    (2) Folding semantics per YAML 1.2 §8.1.1.2: non-blank line runs join with a space; blank lines become literal paragraph-break newlines.
    (3) Block scalar content lines are collected raw during tokenization (`collectBlockScalar`/`detectBlockScalarIndicator` in lib/yamlOps.js) *before* comment-stripping or mapping/sequence parsing ever sees them — so `#` and `key: value`-shaped lines inside a block scalar are correctly preserved as literal text, never treated as a comment or nested structure.
    (4) Smoke-tested the carried-over `_smoke.js` (13 ad-hoc cases) — all passed — confirming the implementation itself was sound; the gap was test-suite integration, not correctness.
    (5) Replaced the scratch script with a proper rigor-leveled suite: new `test/sections/07-block-scalars.js` (24 tests: Normal — literal/folded happy path via the real `query_data` tool integration path, not just direct `parseYaml` calls; Medium — all three chomping modes, explicit indent digit, empty block content; High — block-end-at-dedented-sibling boundary, EOF-terminated block, folded paragraph breaks, 3-level-deep nesting; Critical — shell/SQL-injection-shaped content round-tripping literally, path traversal still blocked, YAML-looking lines inside a literal block confirmed NOT parsed as structure; Extreme — 5000-line block scalar performance, concurrent reads, fuzz bytes after a block indicator, malformed indicator fallback). Wired into `test/run-tests.js` as section [11]. Full suite: **155 passed, 0 failed** (131 prior + 24 new).
    (6) Updated `lib/toolsSchema.js` `query_data` description and README's `query_data` bullet to move block scalars (`|`/`>`) from the "not supported" list to the supported-feature description (file header comment in lib/yamlOps.js already documented this correctly).
    (7) Cleanup: deleted 9 stray `.bak` files (gitignored backup artifacts accumulated by `write_file`'s auto-backup-on-whole-file-replace across this and prior sessions: executeTool.js.bak, processOps.js.bak, roots.js.bak, toolsSchema.js.bak, yamlOps.js.bak, README.md.bak, task.md.bak, run-tests.js.bak, 06-audit-fixes.js.bak) and the scratch `_smoke.js`. `.gitignore` already covers `*.bak`, no change needed there.
    All lib/ and test/ files remain under the 500-line threshold (largest: lib/yamlOps.js at 486 lines).

- [x] Extend git tools: add `git_diff` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented this session. `gitDiff()` added to lib/gitOps.js — calls `git diff` with four modes: working-tree vs HEAD (default), staged/index vs HEAD (`staged=true`), working-tree vs a specific ref (`from_ref` only), and commit-to-commit (`from_ref` + `to_ref`). Optional `file` argument restricts diff to a single path. All ref/file args validated via `assertSafeArg` (shell-metachar + length guard same as git_status/log/blame). Returns: `{ fromRef, toRef, staged, file, unified, additions, deletions, hunks, changedFiles: [{status, path}] }`. Status codes in changedFiles reflect A(dded), D(eleted), R(enamed), M(odified) detected from the unified diff header lines. Schema added to toolsSchema.js; dispatch case added to executeTool.js; `git_diff` added to execute_pipeline enum. New test/sections/12-git-diff.js — 27 tests (Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme): clean-tree empty diff, unstaged/staged detection, commit-to-commit, file filter, field completeness, single-ref mode, bad-ref / non-git-dir error handling, semicolon/backtick/pipe/dollar/newline injection rejection, 4097-char arg rejection, path traversal blocking, 500-line all-lines-replaced large diff, 10 concurrent consistent calls, JSON-serialisability, multi-file detection, cleanup. Full suite: **289 passed, 0 failed** (262 prior + 27 new). All lib/ and test/ files remain under 500 lines.

- [x] Proactive: add `read_archive` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented (previous session committed archiveOps.js + schema/dispatch but session cut off before final commit + task update). lib/archiveOps.js (166 lines) — pure Node.js ZIP Central Directory reader (no npm deps): scans EOCD record, walks CDFH headers, decodes DOS timestamps to ISO 8601, resolves compression method names, returns structured manifest with fileCount/totalUncompressedBytes/totalCompressedBytes/entries. Returns { path, fileCount, totalUncompressedBytes, totalCompressedBytes, entries[] } where each entry has { name, isDirectory, size, compressedSize, compressionMethod, crc32, lastModified }. Schema already in toolsSchema.js, dispatch already in executeTool.js, `read_archive` already in execute_pipeline enum. test/sections/13-read-archive.js — 31 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme including synthetic hand-crafted ZIP (directory entry with isDirectory=true), 200-entry ZIP, 100KB large-file compressed-size check, concurrent reads, JSON-serializability, path-traversal/injection blocking, EOCD-not-found errors, null-byte path rejection. Full suite: **320 passed, 0 failed** (289 prior + 31 new). README entry for read_archive already present in toolsSchema. Cleaned 7 stray .bak files.

- [x] Proactive: add `git_stash_list` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented across two sessions (previous session was cut off after writing the implementation + tests but before running the suite, committing, or updating this file — left lib/gitOpsHelpers.js, lib/gitStashOps.js, test/sections/14-git-stash-list.js untracked plus modified lib/executeTool.js/lib/gitOps.js/lib/toolsSchema.js/test/run-tests.js uncommitted). Verified this session: extracted lib/gitOpsHelpers.js (`gitExec`, `assertSafeArg`, `q`) out of lib/gitOps.js so it can be shared with the new lib/gitStashOps.js without duplicating the shell-safety helpers (gitOps.js shrank from ~410+66 to 410 lines as a result, still well under 500). `gitStashList(repoDir)` runs `git log -g refs/stash` with a unit/record-separator format string (`%gs`/`%an`/`%ae`/`%aI`), parses it into `{ count, stashes: [{ index, ref: "stash@{N}", message, author, email, date }] }`, most-recent-first (matching git's natural stash ordering), and returns `{ count: 0, stashes: [] }` (not an error) when the repo has no stash ref yet. Wired into lib/executeTool.js dispatch, lib/toolsSchema.js (schema + execute_pipeline enum), and test/run-tests.js. 22 tests in test/sections/14-git-stash-list.js across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (field shape/types, stash@{N} ordering and index correctness, ISO date validation, empty-stash boundary, non-git-dir and missing-repo error handling, path traversal + absolute-path-outside-root blocking, JSON-serialisability, no-prototype-pollution, injection-shaped messages round-tripping literally, 5-stash stress case, 10 concurrent reads, 50 repeat reads, fixture cleanup). README "Git Metadata Tools" section and Code Layout table updated (git_stash_list bullet, "four"→"five" never-require-exec sentence, new gitOpsHelpers.js/gitStashOps.js rows). Cleaned 2 stray `.bak` files left by write_file's auto-backup. Full suite: **343 passed, 0 failed** (320 prior + 23 new in test/sections/14-git-stash-list.js).

- [x] Proactive: add `find_duplicates` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented this session. New lib/duplicateOps.js (133 lines, kept separate from lib/utilOps.js which was already at 489/500 lines) — `findDuplicates(rootDir, alias, opts)` walks the directory recursively (respecting MCP_IGNORE via `isIgnored`/`clientRelative` from lib/roots.js), then uses a two-pass size-prefilter strategy for performance: (1) group all candidate files by exact byte size — a file with a size unique in the tree can never be a duplicate of anything and is never hashed; (2) only files sharing a size with at least one sibling are hashed (MD5/SHA-1/SHA-256 default/SHA-512, reusing the same algorithm allow-list convention as `file_checksum`). Returns `{ algorithm, filesScanned, filesHashed, duplicateSetCount, totalDuplicateFiles, totalWastedBytes, duplicateSets: [{ hash, size, count, wastedBytes, files: [sorted relPaths] }] }`, sets sorted by `wastedBytes` descending (most disk-space-impactful first) — directly useful for the "disk-space audits and deduplication" use case from the original task note. Optional `extensions` filter and `min_size` (bytes) filter to narrow noisy scans (e.g. exclude empty files). Schema added to lib/toolsSchema.js (no required fields — `path` defaults to "." like `search_files`/`find_files`), dispatch case added to lib/executeTool.js, `find_duplicates` added to the `execute_pipeline` enum. New test/sections/15-find-duplicates.js — 30 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme: duplicate-set shape/fields, wastedBytes math, alphabetical file sorting, empty/single-file boundaries, invalid algorithm + negative min_size validation, extensions/min_size filtering, same-size-but-different-content correctly NOT flagged (verifies the two-pass logic has no false positives), non-existent-directory and file-as-path error handling, MCP_IGNORE (`node_modules`) directories skipped, cross-subdirectory duplicate detection, path traversal + absolute-path-outside-root blocking, JSON-serialisability, no-prototype-pollution, shell/SQL-injection-shaped content and an injection-shaped `algorithm` value both handled as literal/rejected data (never executed), a 40-file/10-pair stress case, 200KB identical-file hashing, 15-file random-fuzz-content run with a no-false-positive assertion, and 10 concurrent scans returning consistent results. README "Utility Tools" bullet and Code Layout table row added. Full suite: **373 passed, 0 failed** (343 prior + 30 new). All lib/ and test/ files remain under 500 lines (largest: lib/utilOps.js at 489).

- [x] Proactive: add `compare_directories` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented and verified this session (previous session created lib/compareOps.js, test/sections/16-compare-directories.js, and wired up executeTool.js/toolsSchema.js/README.md/test/run-tests.js but was cut off before committing). compareDirectories(leftDir, rightDir, opts) collects all files relative to each tree root using collectRelative (skipping MCP_IGNORE'd dirs like node_modules), then groups by relPath and classifies into added/removed/modified/unchanged using a two-phase check: (1) size comparison (fast statSync) and (2) content hash (md5/sha1/sha256 default/sha512 via crypto). Returns { algorithm, leftFileCount, rightFileCount, added, removed, modified, unchanged (all arrays, sorted), summary: { addedCount, removedCount, modifiedCount, unchangedCount } } plus the echoed left/right args. Path jail enforced by resolveClientPath for both left and right. 28 tests in test/sections/16-compare-directories.js (Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme). Full suite: **401 passed, 0 failed** (373 prior + 28 new). All lib/ and test/ files remain under 500 lines.

- [x] Proactive: add `count_lines` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented in lib/wc.js (75 lines). `countLines(absPaths, origPaths)` reads each file as a Buffer, counts `\n` bytes for line count (no-trailing-newline files get +1), splits UTF-8 text on whitespace for word count. Returns `{ files: [{path, lines, words, bytes}], total: {lines, words, bytes} }`. Schema added to toolsSchema.js (required: paths array), dispatch in executeTool.js with an explicit non-empty array guard. 38 tests in test/sections/17-new-tools.js (section [21]) covering Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme alongside file_tree and hash_directory — all 439 passing.

- [x] Proactive: add `file_tree` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented in lib/treeOps.js (100 lines). `fileTree(baseDir, origPath, opts)` walks the directory using `readdirSync`, filters out MCP_IGNORE'd names, sorts dirs-first-then-files alphabetically at each level, and emits Unicode box-drawing connectors (`├──`, `└──`, `│`). Supports `depth` (1–10, default 4) and `sizes` (annotate each file with its byte count). Truncates at 500 nodes (sets `truncated: true` and appends a note to the tree string). Returns `{ path, tree, dirCount, fileCount, truncated }`. Included in section [21] tests: ASCII structure verified, depth limit, sizes annotation, node_modules exclusion, truncation at 501+ files, path traversal blocked. All 439 tests passing.

- [x] Proactive: add `hash_directory` tool — status: tested
  - notes: Implemented in lib/hashDirOps.js (103 lines). `hashDirectory(absDir, origPath, opts)` walks the tree via `readdirSync`, skips MCP_IGNORE'd entries, collects `{relPath, absPath}` pairs, sorts by `relPath` for determinism, then feeds each `relPath + '\0' + fileContent` into a rolling crypto hash (md5/sha1/sha256 default/sha512). Returns `{ path, algorithm, hash, fileCount, totalBytes }`. Hash changes on any add/remove/rename/modify. Optional `extensions` filter. Included in section [21] tests: determinism across repeated calls, hash changes on file add and content modify, empty-dir stability, extensions filter, md5/sha512 variants, invalid-algo rejection, path traversal blocked, 10 concurrent calls consistent, 100KB file. All 439 tests passing.

Found and fixed one real bug during verification: `base64_decode`'s round-trip validation did not strip whitespace before comparing, so a perfectly valid base64 string wrapped across multiple lines (e.g. MIME-style 76-char wrapping, or just a value copy-pasted with line breaks) was incorrectly rejected as "not valid base64". Fixed by stripping all whitespace from the normalised input before decoding and before the round-trip comparison. Also added a `typeof b64Data !== "string"` guard for a clearer error on bad input types. Currently finishing: test coverage (5 rigor levels) + README + line-count split of toolsSchema.js/executeTool.js (both had crept to 509/511 lines, over the 500-line threshold) + commit.
- [x] Proactive: add `base64_encode`/`base64_decode`, `json_format`, `text_transform` tools — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off mid-implementation with uncommitted lib/encodingOps.js + lib/textOps.js as untracked files, plus uncommitted edits to lib/executeTool.js/lib/toolsSchema.js and no test coverage or README update). - [x] Proactive: audit move_file/copy_file in lib/fileOps.js for cross-root/symlink/EXDEV edge cases — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off mid-audit: lib/moveOps.js, test/sections/25-move-copy-ops.js, and test/sections/25b-move-copy-ops-cde.js existed as untracked/uncommitted files, plus uncommitted dispatchWrite.js/writeSchemas.js wiring, but the two new test files were never required into test/run-tests.js, never run, and never committed). On review the implementation itself (lib/moveOps.js, 178 lines) was already functionally complete and well-reasoned — five issues audited and fixed vs the original lib/fileOps.js move_file/copy_file: (1) **symlink escape** — a symlink living inside a jailed root that points outside it would previously be silently followed by fs.renameSync/copyFileSync; fixed via `assertRealpathWithinRoot()`, which realpath-resolves the nearest existing ancestor of both source and destination (and the target itself, if it already exists) and rejects with a -32001-coded error if it falls outside the owning root. (2) **EXDEV (cross-device move)** — fs.renameSync throws EXDEV when source/destination are on different drives/filesystems (a real scenario since MCP_ROOTS can span multiple Windows drive letters); fixed with a copy+unlink fallback specifically on `e.code === "EXDEV"`, surfaced in the result as `crossDevice: true/false`. (3) **overwrite safety** — neither tool previously checked if the destination already existed, silently clobbering it; fixed with an explicit `overwrite` option (default false) that throws a clear -32602 ToolError, mirroring create_file's existing convention. (4) **directory source rejection** — passing a directory as source used to surface a raw OS error (EISDIR / silent directory rename); fixed with an explicit upfront isDirectory check and a clear -32602 error for both tools. (5) **same-path no-op** — moving/copying a path to itself is now an explicit `{ noop: true }` short-circuit rather than relying on incidental, OS-dependent rename/copy-to-self behavior (Windows treats these differently between rename and copy, and copy-to-self can corrupt a file mid-copy in rare cases). Wired lib/moveOps.js's `moveFile`/`copyFile` into lib/dispatchWrite.js (replacing the old inline fs.renameSync/copyFileSync calls), added `overwrite` to both schemas in lib/schemas/writeSchemas.js. Found and fixed one real bug in the test suite itself during verification: a Critical-level test asserted that the client-path string `"/tmp/malicious-src.txt"` must be rejected by `resolveClientPath` as "outside root" — but a single leading slash is this server's alias-relative client-path convention (stripped before resolution), not a real OS-absolute path, so on this Windows-hosted jail it correctly normalizes to `tmp/malicious-src.txt` *inside* the root rather than escaping — the test's assumption only held on a hypothetical POSIX layout where `/tmp` is a real top-level absolute path. Replaced it with a test that asserts the actually-correct security property (the resolved path stays contained inside the root for this input), keeping the genuine escape-vector tests (`..` traversal, real OS-absolute path with a drive letter / unmatched alias, symlink escape) unchanged alongside it. Wired both new test files into test/run-tests.js as sections [28-ABC] and [28-DE] (were on disk but never required in — the actual point where the previous session was cut off). 36 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (happy-path move/copy incl. nested-directory auto-creation and overwrite, missing-source/existing-destination/directory-source validation errors, same-path no-op, large 100KB + binary + empty + Unicode-filename + 240-char-filename copies, 10 concurrent + 50 sequential copies, symlink-escape blocking, path traversal blocking, injection-shaped filenames treated as literal, null-byte path handling, fuzz bytes, JSON-serialisability, no prototype pollution). Cleaned 4 stray .bak files (writeSchemas.js.bak, dispatchWrite.js.bak, task.md.bak, plus 2 more generated by this session's own replace_in_file calls on README.md and 25b-move-copy-ops-cde.js). README updated: move_file/copy_file bullet rewritten to document the audited behavior (overwrite flag, EXDEV fallback, symlink protection, same-path no-op), new lib/moveOps.js row added to the Code Layout table. Full suite: **674 passed, 0 failed** (639 prior + 36 new − 1 net, since one prior test was rewritten in place rather than added). All lib/ and test/ files remain under the 500-line threshold (largest: test/sections/25-move-copy-ops.js at 300 lines).

- [x] Proactive: add `move_directory`/`copy_directory` tools — recursive-tree variants built on the audited lib/moveOps.js primitives — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off after writing lib/moveDirOps.js and wiring dispatchWrite.js/writeSchemas.js/execSchemas.js/toolsSchema.js, but before writing tests, updating the README, or committing). On review the implementation (lib/moveDirOps.js, 203 lines) was already functionally complete and well-reasoned — no bugs found. `walkTree(dir)` recursively collects forward-slash relative `files`/`dirs` lists (parent-before-child), skipping MCP_IGNORE'd entries, and throws a -32001 ToolError immediately if *any* symlink is found anywhere in the source tree — by design, no partial/silent-skip for a multi-file operation (a half-applied recursive copy/move is worse than none at all). `validateDirOp()` shares the audited `assertRealpathWithinRoot` check from lib/moveOps.js for both source and destination, rejects non-directory/missing sources, and enforces an explicit `overwrite` policy (default false) on the destination, mirroring move_file/copy_file conventions. `moveDirectory()` tries a fast whole-tree `fs.renameSync` first when the destination doesn't already exist, falling back to recursive copy+delete on `EXDEV` (cross-device) or whenever merging into an existing destination (`overwrite: true`) — returns `{ moved, noop, crossDevice, merged, strategy: "rename"|"copy+delete", filesCopied?, directoriesCreated?, totalBytes? }`. `copyDirectory()` always does a full recursive copy, leaving the source untouched, returns `{ copied, noop, merged, filesCopied, directoriesCreated, totalBytes }`. Same-path moves/copies short-circuit as `{ noop: true }`. Wired into lib/dispatchWrite.js (`move_directory`/`copy_directory` handlers), lib/schemas/writeSchemas.js (schemas with required source+destination, optional overwrite), lib/schemas/execSchemas.js (execute_pipeline enum) — all already correct on review, no fixes needed. New test/sections/27-move-copy-dir-ops.js (317 lines, Normal/Medium/High) + test/sections/27b-move-copy-dir-ops-de.js (227 lines, Critical/Extreme) — split from the start to stay under the 500-line threshold (the combined draft was 508 lines). 32 tests across all 5 rigor levels: nested-tree copy/move happy path (including the fast-rename vs copy+delete-fallback strategy fields), parent-directory auto-creation, empty-dir handling, missing-source/file-as-source/destination-exists-without-overwrite validation errors, same-path no-op, overwrite:true merge semantics (colliding files overwritten, non-colliding files preserved on both move and copy), `walkTree` ordering/shape, MCP_IGNORE (node_modules) skipping, path traversal + absolute-path-outside-root blocking, whole-tree symlink-escape abort-before-write guarantee (skips gracefully if symlink creation needs elevated privileges, same convention as the move_file/copy_file audit), injection-shaped directory/file names treated as literal paths, deep destination jailing, 10-level-deep nesting, 100-file wide tree, 200KB binary file, 10 concurrent copies, 50-file fast-rename move, Unicode/emoji names, JSON-serialisability + no prototype pollution. Wired into test/run-tests.js as sections [30-ABC]/[30-DE]. Full suite: **726 passed, 0 failed** (694 prior + 32 new). - [x] Proactive: add `http_fetch` tool — make HTTP/HTTPS GET/POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE requests from the server (useful for API calls, health checks, webhook triggers) — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session implemented lib/httpFetchOps.js (zero-dep http/https, redirect following up to 5 hops with loop detection, 100KB body truncation, scheme validation, control-char rejection), wired schemas/dispatch/pipeline-enum, and rewired executeTool.js/executePipeline/handleMessage/server-http.js/server-stdio.js to be fully async — execute_pipeline now `await`s each step so async tools like http_fetch resolve to real values instead of dangling Promises — but was cut off with test/sections/29-http-fetch.js complete (32 tests) while its sibling test/sections/29b-http-fetch-pipeline.js, referenced in test/run-tests.js as the execute_pipeline+http_fetch integration suite, was a 0-byte empty file; also left an empty scratch file `_repro_timeout.js` at the repo root). This session: (1) wrote test/sections/29b-http-fetch-pipeline.js — 9 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme covering: a single http_fetch pipeline step resolving a real object (not a dangling Promise — the literal bug this async rewrite fixes), sync-then-async step ordering, missing-required-field per-step errors with both `on_error: stop` and `on_error: continue`, multiple sequential http_fetch steps to different paths with no cross-contamination, a failing bad-scheme step under `on_error: continue` not aborting later steps with a JSON-serialisable plain-string error, 10 concurrent 2-step pipelines, and 5-step pipelines confirming no `[object Promise]` ever leaks into a JSON.stringify'd result. (2) Ran the full suite and hit a **real, deterministic (not flaky) bug**: the first http_fetch test in both [32] and [32b] failed every run with `request timed out after 15s` even though the local loopback test server answers instantly. Root cause: `test/run-tests.js` required all sections in a flat sequence and only awaited the async ones (01/08/29/29b) via a single `Promise.all(...)` at the very end — so each async section's IIFE started running the moment it was required and then had to compete with every *synchronous* section's `require()` (02 through 28), which collectively block the single-threaded event loop for tens of seconds doing real CPU/IO work (5000-line files, 2000-row CSVs, hashing, etc.). The in-flight HTTP request's response was sitting unprocessed while the main thread was busy, so by the time the event loop got back to it the request's own 15s timer (which *does* fire on schedule via libuv) had already elapsed in wall-clock time. Fixed by rewriting test/run-tests.js's body into an `async main()` that `await`s each async section's exported promise **immediately after requiring it**, before requiring the next section — this serializes execution (no loss of real parallelism, since none of this work was ever actually concurrent CPU work to begin with) and guarantees no async section's network/timer activity has to race a synchronous section's blocking work. Re-ran the full suite twice after the fix: **803 passed, 0 failed** both times (was 801/2 failed before — net +2 from the new section 32b cleanup test and the previously-uncounted-as-failing-but-now-fixed first http_fetch test). (3) Deleted 18 stray `.bak` files and the empty `_repro_timeout.js` scratch file. (4) README updated: version v3.9.0 → v3.10.0, new `http_fetch` bullet under Utility Tools documenting method/headers/body/timeout/redirect/truncation behavior and the execute_pipeline-await guarantee, new `lib/httpFetchOps.js` row in the Code Layout table. All lib/ and test/ files remain under the 500-line threshold (largest: test/sections/29-http-fetch.js at 447 lines).

- [x] Proactive: add `yaml_merge` tool — merge two YAML documents (base + patch) using deep-merge semantics — status: tested
  - notes: Completed across two sessions. Previous session implemented lib/yamlMergeOps.js (135 lines, pure non-mutating deepMerge + yamlMerge wrapper), wired it into lib/dispatchWrite.js/lib/schemas/writeSchemas.js/lib/schemas/execSchemas.js/lib/toolsSchema.js, and wrote test/sections/31-yaml-merge.js (all 5 rigor levels in one file, 34-A through 34-E) — but was cut off after a test run showed 4 failures, all in the new test file's own fixtures (not the implementation): (1) [34-B-6]/[34-B-7] used a base/patch fixture `": not valid: : yaml\n"` that this repo's minimal YAML parser actually accepted instead of rejecting; (2) [34-B-8] assumed a bare scalar root document (`"just a string\n"`) is valid YAML, but lib/yamlOps.js only supports mapping/sequence/null roots and throws "expected 'key: value'" for bare scalars; (3) [34-D-1] used an injection fixture containing a literal `#` (`"; rm -rf / #"`) which is plausible to be mis-parsed as a trailing comment by an unquoted-scalar serializer path. This session: (1) fixed [34-B-6]/[34-B-7] to reuse the project's established "no colon" invalid-YAML fixture (`"this is not valid yaml\n"`, same pattern as test/sections/05-yaml-query.js); (2) replaced the bare-scalar-root premise of [34-B-8] — first tried an empty flow-mapping patch (`"{}\n"`), discovered that ALSO isn't a supported root form by this parser (same "expected 'key: value'" error), and settled on a true boundary case instead: a patch that re-asserts an already-identical value, confirming the merge is a real no-op when nothing actually changes; (3) fixed [34-D-1] to use the already-proven-safe injection patterns from test/sections/30b-yaml-patch-de.js's [33-D-2]/[33-D-3] (`"'; DROP TABLE users; --"` and `"$(rm -rf /)"`) instead of a `#`-containing string. Re-ran the full suite after each fix; final run: **891 passed, 0 failed** (853 prior + 38 new yaml_merge tests across 34-A through 34-E: 9 Normal incl. recursive-merge/array-replace/dry-run/pure-function-no-mutation; 8 Medium param validation incl. missing/empty/whitespace/non-string patch, missing base file, invalid YAML in either side; 7 High mismatched-shape behavior incl. mapping↔scalar↔array replace-not-merge and explicit-null semantics; 7 Critical security incl. shell/SQL-injection-shaped values, HTML/script content, `__proto__` pollution attempt, JSON-serialisability, unicode/emoji; 7 Extreme incl. 1000-key base doc, 10-level-deep nested patch, 50 sequential merges, 10 concurrent dry-runs, fuzz bytes, 500-item array). Deleted 7 stray `.bak` files left by `replace_in_file` calls across both sessions (lib/schemas/execSchemas.js.bak, lib/schemas/writeSchemas.js.bak, lib/dispatchWrite.js.bak, lib/toolsSchema.js.bak, test/sections/31-yaml-merge.js.bak, test/run-tests.js.bak, task.md.bak). - [x] Proactive: add `json_query` tool extension — support JSONPath-style wildcards ($.a[*].b) in `query_json` / `query_data` — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off after implementing lib/jsonPathOps.js and wiring lib/dispatchRead.js/lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js/lib/schemas/execSchemas.js/test/run-tests.js, but before writing the README section or committing — test/sections/33-query-path.js was already present and complete). On review the implementation (lib/jsonPathOps.js, 294 lines) was already functionally complete and correct — no bugs found. Implements a new `query_path` tool: a zero-dep tokenizer + recursive evaluator supporting `$` (root), `.key`/`['key']`/`[\"key\"]` (child access), `[N]` (array index), `[*]` (wildcard over array/object children), and `..` (recursive descent / deep-scan with remainder-of-path applied at every depth). Guards: max recursion depth 50, max result count 10,000, max query length 2000 chars — all enforced via `ToolError(-32602)`. Auto-detects JSON vs YAML by file extension (reuses `parseYaml` from lib/yamlOps.js for `.yaml`/`.yml`), override via explicit `format` arg. Single match returned as scalar, multiple matches as an array (mirrors `query_json`/`query_data` ergonomics). Returns `{ path, query, format, matchCount, truncated, result }`. All wiring already correct on review: dispatch handler in lib/dispatchRead.js, schema in lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js, `query_path` already in the execute_pipeline op enum in lib/schemas/execSchemas.js, section [36] already required in test/run-tests.js. 44 tests in test/sections/33-query-path.js across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (root/dot-path/index/wildcard/recursive-descent/bracket-notation happy paths, YAML auto-detect, missing-path -32602, query-optional behavior, non-existent-file/invalid-JSON/invalid-YAML errors, no-match→empty-array+matchCount=0, out-of-bounds index, invalid format, malformed JSONPath syntax errors, mixed object+array deep scan, null/boolean value handling, chained wildcards, explicit format override on non-standard extension, path traversal + absolute-path-outside-root blocked, 2000-char query length limit, injection-shaped key names via bracket notation handled as literal data, shell-metacharacter format value rejected, `__proto__` key non-pollution, JSON-serialisability, no-unexpected-keys check, 1000-item array `[*]`, 20-level-deep traversal, 10 concurrent calls, recursive-descent performance on a 243-leaf tree, fuzz/malformed-query non-crash check, execute_pipeline op-enum registration check, cleanup). Full suite: **968 passed, 0 failed** (924 prior + 44 new). - [x] Proactive: add `json_query`/`query_path` support for array slice syntax `[start:end]` (e.g. `$.items[0:3]`) — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session. Extended lib/jsonPathOps.js's bracket-content tokenizer with a new `T_SLICE` token type covering `[start:end]`, `[start:]`, `[:end]`, and `[:]` forms, with optional signed (negative) integers on either side. Evaluation: negative indices count from the end of the array (`len + n`, clamped to 0), positive indices clamp to array length, `start >= end` (including the empty/reversed-range case) yields zero matches rather than throwing. A slice applied to a non-array node (object, scalar) silently yields no matches, consistent with how `[N]`/`[*]` already behave on type-mismatched nodes. Slices compose with everything else in the engine — chaining a slice into a subsequent `.key` access (`$.a[1:3].x`) or nesting a slice 2+ levels deep all work via the same `applySteps` recursion used for wildcards. A slice that happens to capture exactly one element still follows the engine's existing single-match-unwraps-to-scalar convention (matchCount===1 → scalar `result`), for consistency with `[N]`/`.key`/wildcard semantics rather than introducing a special case. Malformed slice syntax (missing closing bracket, double colon, non-numeric bounds, shell-injection-shaped bound strings) all throw `ToolError(-32602)` at parse time before any evaluation — the slice bounds are never passed to anything that could interpret them as code. New test/sections/33b-query-path-slice.js — 27 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme: all four slice forms, negative-start/negative-end/both-negative, chained field access after a slice, empty-array/out-of-bounds/start===end/start>end boundary behavior, slice-on-non-array no-match, malformed-syntax rejections, YAML-sourced documents, 2-level nesting, single-element-slice scalar-unwrap convention, path traversal still blocked, non-numeric and shell-injection-shaped bounds rejected at parse time, JSON-serialisability, 1000-item large-array slice, 10 concurrent calls, assorted fuzz/malformed slice-shaped queries that must not crash the process, cleanup. Wired into test/run-tests.js as section [36b]. Full suite: **995 passed, 0 failed** (968 prior + 27 new). README updated: version v3.14.0 → v3.15.0, `query_path` bullet extended to document `[start:end]` slice support, `lib/jsonPathOps.js` Code Layout row updated. Schema description in lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js updated to mention slice syntax. Cleaned stray `.bak`/scratch files.

- [x] Proactive: add a `find_replace_dir` / bulk text-replace tool that runs `replace_in_file`-style find/replace across every matching file under a directory tree in one call (currently the existing find/replace lives only on the single-file `apply_patch`/`json_patch`/`yaml_patch` family, with no batch-across-a-tree primitive) — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off mid-implementation: uncommitted edits to lib/fileOps.js/lib/dispatchWrite.js/lib/schemas/writeSchemas.js/test/run-tests.js plus an untracked test/sections/34-find-replace-dir.js, no test run, no commit). On review, `replace_in_file` already supported directory-tree mode from an earlier session (recursive walk, extensions filter) — this task's actual gap was `dry_run` support plus dedicated test coverage, which is what the previous session had been adding. `replaceInSingleFile()` in lib/fileOps.js gained an `opts.dryRun` flag (preview replacement counts/sizes without writing or creating `.bak`), and a real regex-mode bug was fixed at the same time: the old implementation used `original.replace(re, (...args) => { count++; return replace; })` — a callback form that ignores `$1`/`$2` capture-group syntax in the replacement string entirely (they'd be inserted as literal text, not substituted), contradicting the tool's own documented "$1, $2 etc. for capture groups" schema description. Fixed by switching to the native `String#replace(RegExp, replacementString)` form so the engine itself performs capture-group substitution, with match count computed separately via `original.match(re)`. `dispatchWrite.js`'s `replace_in_file` handler threads `dry_run` through to both the single-file and directory-walk code paths and echoes `dryRun` in the result. Schema updated in `lib/schemas/writeSchemas.js` (new `dry_run` boolean property, description rewritten to document bulk-directory-mode + dry-run behavior). New test/sections/34-find-replace-dir.js — 24 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (literal + regex-with-capture-groups replace across a tree, extensions filter, dry_run leaves disk untouched, result-shape checks, empty-directory/no-match boundaries, single-file-path back-compat, missing search/replace still throws, mid-scan-deleted-file handled independently, non-existent-directory error, nested subdirectories walked, path traversal + absolute-path-outside-root blocked, shell/SQL-injection-shaped search/replace round-trip literally, dry_run-never-mutates-even-with-real-matches, JSON-serialisability, no prototype pollution, 40-file stress case, 10 concurrent dry_run scans, fuzz bytes as search/replace). **Bug found and fixed during verification (Tester role):** the Extreme-level "ReDoS-shaped regex pattern" test as originally written used a genuinely exponential-time nested-quantifier pattern (`(a+)+$` against input not ending in the repeated char) — this is true V8 catastrophic backtracking, not just "slow," and hung `test/run-tests.js` indefinitely (confirmed by running it standalone and having to kill the process after 90+ seconds of no progress). Every other regex-adjacent ReDoS test elsewhere in this codebase (test/sections/01-core-ops.js, 20-search-lines.js) deliberately uses an "evil-looking but polynomial" pattern instead (`a+a+a+a+b`-style, not nested) that actually completes in bounded time — replaced the new test's pattern with that same established convention so the assertion is real rather than one that can never fail because it never returns. Full suite re-run after the fix: **1020 passed, 0 failed** (995 prior + 24 new + 1 net from the ReDoS-test rewrite), confirmed via a background process run to avoid the tool-call timeout on this now-large suite (~55s wall time). Cleaned 6 stray `.bak` files and 3 stray `test_output*.txt` log files left by this and prior sessions; added `test_output*.txt` to `.gitignore` to prevent recurrence. - [x] Proactive: add `file_diff_dir` tool — diff two directory trees and show file-level and line-level differences — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off after implementing lib/dirDiffOps.js, wiring dispatchRead.js/utilSchemas.js/execSchemas.js/run-tests.js, and writing test/sections/32-file-diff-dir.js — but before running the suite, updating README, or committing). On review the implementation (lib/dirDiffOps.js, 151 lines) was already functionally complete and correct — no bugs found. `fileDiffDir(leftDir, rightDir, leftClientPath, rightClientPath, opts)` calls `compareDirectories()` to get the file-level classification (added/removed/modified/unchanged), then walks each `modified` entry and calls `diffFiles()` to produce a line-level unified diff. Added and removed files are reported by status only (no "other side" to diff against). Unchanged files are omitted from the per-file list entirely. A `max_diff_lines` budget (default 500, max 5000, clamped not rejected above cap) caps total unified-diff lines across all files combined — once exhausted, remaining modified files are listed bare (status + relPath, no unified text) and `truncated: true` is set. Optional `extensions` filter passed through to compareDirectories. Optional `context` lines (default 3) passed through to diffFiles. Race-condition safety: if a file disappears between the hash-comparison pass and the diff pass, it's reported as "modified-but-undiffable" rather than crashing. Returns `{ left, right, algorithm, leftFileCount, rightFileCount, summary, diffs: [{relPath, status, unified?, additions?, deletions?, hunks?}], maxDiffLines, totalDiffLinesEmitted, truncated }`. All wiring was already in place: dispatch handler in lib/dispatchRead.js, schema in lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js, `file_diff_dir` already in the execute_pipeline op enum in lib/schemas/execSchemas.js, section [35] already required in test/run-tests.js. 33 tests in test/sections/32-file-diff-dir.js across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (added/removed/modified/unchanged classification, real unified diff fields verified, missing left/right -32602, invalid algorithm, non-existent left, file-not-directory for right, max_diff_lines=0 lists-bare+truncated, negative max_diff_lines -32602, cap clamping, extensions filter, empty-left all-added, empty-right all-removed, budget partially-exhausted mid-list, node_modules MCP_IGNORE skipped on both sides, path traversal left+right blocked, absolute-OS-path blocked, injection-shaped content literal in diff output, injection-shaped algorithm rejected, JSON-serialisable, no prototype pollution, 30-file deterministic mix, 500-line large file, 10 concurrent calls consistent, nested subdirectories correct relPath, fuzz binary content does not crash, cleanup). Full suite: **924 passed, 0 failed** (891 prior + 33 new). README updated: version v3.12.0 → v3.13.0, new `file_diff_dir` bullet under Utility Tools documenting the tool's output shape and budget/truncation behavior, new `lib/dirDiffOps.js` row in the Code Layout table. Cleaned stray `.bak` files.

- [x] Proactive: add a `git_show` tool — read a file's content as of a specific commit/ref without checking it out — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off after implementing the tool end-to-end — `gitShow`+`gitExecBuffer` in lib/gitOps.js/lib/gitOpsHelpers.js, dispatch wiring in lib/dispatchRead.js, schema in lib/schemas/gitSchemas.js, execute_pipeline enum entry in lib/schemas/execSchemas.js — but before writing test/sections/36-git-show.js (left as a 0-byte untracked file), running the suite, updating the README, or committing; all 5 modified lib/ files were uncommitted). On review the implementation itself needed no fixes — logic was sound: `gitShow(repoDir, ref, filePath)` resolves `ref` (blank/omitted → `"HEAD"`, trimmed) to a full 40-char commit hash via `git rev-parse <ref>^{commit}` first (unknown ref → clear "unknown ref" error, not a raw git stderr blob), then checks the object type at `<hash>:<file>` via `git cat-file -t` to distinguish a missing path from a path that resolves to a directory (tree) before attempting to read it — both surface descriptive, distinguishing errors rather than one opaque failure. Content is read via a new `gitExecBuffer()` helper (raw `Buffer` stdout, no utf8 coercion, 50MB cap) specifically so binary blobs aren't corrupted/crashed on before binary-detection even runs; binary is detected via a NUL-byte-in-first-8000-bytes scan (the same heuristic git/most diff tools use) — `isBinary: true` + `content: null` in that case, with `size` still reported. - [x] Proactive: add `csv_query` aggregate functions — sum/avg/count/min/max by group (e.g. `group_by` + `aggregate` params) — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off mid-implementation: uncommitted edits to lib/csvOps.js/lib/dispatchRead.js/lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js plus an untracked test/sections/37-csv-aggregate.js, no test run, no commit). On review the implementation (lib/csvOps.js aggregate extension) was already functionally complete and correct — no bugs found. A non-empty `aggregate` array of `{column, op}` entries (op ∈ sum/avg/count/min/max, strict allow-list via `validateAggregateSpec`) switches `csv_query` into grouped-summary mode; optional `group_by` (column name) groups rows first, otherwise the whole filtered table is one implicit group. `count` may omit `column` (counts rows) or supply one (counts non-empty values). sum/avg/min/max require `column` and throw a clear `ToolError(-32602)` on any non-numeric cell (`parseNumericCell`) rather than silently producing NaN. Duplicate result-field names (`<op>_<column>`, or bare `count`) are rejected up front. Groups are sorted deterministically by group key (`aggregateRows`); `offset`/`limit` paginate over the returned groups instead of raw rows. Non-aggregate mode is untouched and fully backward compatible (only triggered by a non-empty `aggregate` array — a non-array or empty array falls through to the original row-projection path). This session: (1) verified all wiring already correct — dispatch passes `group_by`/`aggregate` through in lib/dispatchRead.js, schema (with nested `aggregate` item shape) in lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js; (2) the untracked test/sections/37-csv-aggregate.js (33 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme: whole-table sum/avg/min/max/count, count-with/without-column, group_by multi-aggregate, deterministic group sort, group_by-without-aggregate throws, empty-aggregate-array falls back to row mode, unknown op/missing column/unknown column/duplicate field all throw -32602, offset/limit paginate groups, has_header:false works, non-numeric value throws not NaN, filter applied before aggregation, all-filtered-out yields zero groups, non-existent file throws, all-blank column throws not NaN/0, path traversal blocked, injection-shaped group keys round-trip literally, non-object/non-array aggregate entries rejected or fall back correctly, aggregate array >20 entries throws, JSON-serialisable/no prototype pollution, 2000-row 4-bucket stress with verified sums, 300-group pagination, 10 concurrent calls consistent, fuzz garbage aggregate shapes rejected cleanly, cleanup) had not been wired into test/run-tests.js — added `require("./sections/37-csv-aggregate")` as the new final entry plus a header doc-comment line; (3) syntax-checked all 4 touched files (`node -c`); (4) ran the full suite via a background process: **1131 passed, 0 failed** (1098 prior + 33 new). - [x] Proactive: add a `git_show`-style `git_tag_list` tool — list git tags with their target commit, message, and date (currently the server has no way to enumerate tags, a natural companion to the existing `git_branch_list`/`git_stash_list` metadata tools) — status: tested
  - notes: Completed across two sessions. Previous session implemented lib/gitTagOps.js, wired dispatchRead.js/gitSchemas.js/execSchemas.js, and wrote test/sections/38-git-tag-list.js (21 tests) — but ran a first draft that had a real bug: `for-each-ref`'s dereference semantics were backwards. For an annotated tag, `%(subject)`/`%(creatordate)` (no `*` prefix) already describe the tag object's OWN message/tagger-date — for-each-ref is formatting the ref's own object (the tag), not the commit it points at. Only `%(objectname)` needed the dereferenced `%(*objectname)` form to resolve to the target commit hash instead of the tag object's own hash. The first draft used the dereferenced (`*`-prefixed) form for subject/date as well, which pulled the *target commit's* message/date instead of the tag's own annotation — caught by two failing tests (`annotated tag reports isAnnotated=true, its own message...` and the injection round-trip test, both asserting the tag's own message and getting the commit's "initial commit" subject instead). Fixed by dropping `%(*subject)`/`%(*creatordate)` entirely and using the plain `%(subject)`/`%(creatordate:iso-strict)` fields for both tag kinds (correct for lightweight tags too, since the ref points straight at the commit in that case) while keeping only `%(*objectname)` for hash resolution. `gitTagList(repoDir)` in the new lib/gitTagOps.js (91 lines) reuses the existing `gitExec`/`q` helpers from lib/gitOpsHelpers.js (no new shell-safety surface). Returns `{ count, tags: [{ name, hash, isAnnotated, date, message }] }`, sorted most-recent-first (matching git_log/git_stash_list convention); empty list (not an error) for a repo with no tags. Wired into lib/dispatchRead.js (`git_tag_list` handler mirroring git_branch_list's `args.path ?? first root` pattern), lib/schemas/gitSchemas.js (schema, optional path), lib/schemas/execSchemas.js (execute_pipeline enum). test/sections/38-git-tag-list.js — 21 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (lightweight vs annotated tag field/hash/message correctness, field shape/types, ISO date validation, no-tags boundary returns empty not error, most-recent-first sort order, multiple tags on the same commit, slash-containing tag names, non-git-dir and unborn-HEAD handled without crashing, no-path-arg defaults to non-git TMP root and throws cleanly, path traversal + absolute-path-outside-root blocked, injection-shaped annotated-tag message round-trips literally via a `-F` message file (never executed), JSON-serialisability, no prototype pollution / no-unexpected-keys on both the result and each tag entry, 15-tag mixed lightweight/annotated stress case, 10 concurrent calls consistent, 50 repeat reads consistent, cleanup). - [x] Proactive: add a `dir_size_stats` utility tool — directory-level disk-usage rollup (like `du -h --max-depth=N`), aggregating bytes per subdirectory rather than the flat per-file top-N that `file_stats` already provides — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session was cut off mid-implementation: uncommitted lib/dirSizeOps.js as an untracked file, plus uncommitted edits to lib/dispatchRead.js/lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js/lib/schemas/execSchemas.js/test/run-tests.js and an untracked test/sections/39-dir-size-stats.js — no test run, no README update, no commit). Which directories are *listed* (not which are counted) is capped by `max_depth` (clamped 1–10, default 2 via a NaN-safe `clampInt` helper that falls back to a safe default for non-finite/garbage-typed input rather than propagating NaN through `Math.min(Math.max(...))`); results sorted by bytes descending and capped at `top_n` (clamped 1–200, default 20). The scanned root itself is never listed as a directory entry (redundant with the top-level totals). Returns `{ path, maxDepth, totalBytes, totalFiles, totalDirs, directories: [{path, depth, bytes, fileCount}] }`. All wiring was already correct on review: dispatch handler in lib/dispatchRead.js (mirrors `file_stats`'s `args.path || "."` default-to-root pattern), schema in lib/schemas/utilSchemas.js, `dir_size_stats` already in the execute_pipeline op enum in lib/schemas/execSchemas.js, section [42] already required in test/run-tests.js. - [x] Proactive: extend `git_log` with an optional `stat`/`include_files` param — per-commit `filesChanged` (or richer `{path, additions, deletions}[]` reusing gitDiffStatOps-style numstat parsing) so an agent can see what each of the last N commits touched without a separate `git_show`/`git_diff` call per commit — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (implemented from scratch — no previous-session artifacts for this task). Added an `includeFiles` param to `gitLog()`: when true, a *second*, minimal `git log --numstat --format=%H<REC>` call (no `%b` body field) is run alongside the existing metadata call, and its per-commit numstat blocks are matched back to each commit by its full 40-hex-char hash (`parseNumstatByHash`, matching on the hash+REC boundary via regex) rather than folded into the single main command — deliberately avoided combining them, since commit bodies can contain arbitrary embedded newlines that would make it ambiguous where one commit's interleaved numstat block ends and the next commit's formatted header begins; a 40-hex-char hash has no such ambiguity. Verified this design empirically with a standalone smoke script against a real 2-commit repo before writing the test suite (exact byte-for-byte match against `git log --numstat`'s own output) and again in the real test suite with a commit whose *subject line itself* is a 40-hex-char string (to rule out the hash-shaped-subject false-positive-boundary edge case) and a commit with a genuine multi-line body. Each commit gets `filesChanged: [{path, additions, deletions}]` (binary files report `additions`/`deletions` as `null`, not `NaN` — same convention as `git_diff`'s existing `stat_only` mode in lib/gitDiffStatOps.js) only when `include_files` is truthy — the key is entirely absent (not an empty array) otherwise, so existing callers/tests see zero behavioral change. Extracted `gitLog`+`parseNumstatByHash` out of lib/gitOps.js into a new lib/gitLogOps.js (gitOps.js had grown to 555 lines after the inline addition, over the 500-line threshold); gitOps.js re-exports `gitLog` via `require("./gitLogOps")` for backward compatibility with existing `require("./gitOps").gitLog` call sites — no dispatcher/schema changes needed beyond the new parameter itself. Wired: lib/dispatchRead.js's `git_log` handler passes `!!args.include_files` through as the 5th positional arg; lib/schemas/gitSchemas.js's `git_log` schema gained an `include_files: boolean` property + description (no execSchemas.js change needed — `git_log` was already in the execute_pipeline op enum, and pipeline steps use `additionalProperties: true`). New test/sections/40-git-log-files.js — 19 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme in its own isolated temp git repo (separate from test/sections/04-git-tools.js's repo, so histories can't interfere): filesChanged present only when include_files=true (and genuinely absent, not `[]`, when omitted), correct per-file add/delete counts across two commits (including a deleted file reporting 0 additions/N deletions and an added file reporting N additions/0 deletions), explicit false === omitted, combined with file-filter and limit, ref=main parity, binary-file null-not-NaN, invalid branch still throws with include_files=true, a genuine 1-commit repo doesn't crash, shell-injection-shaped branch/file still rejected by the existing `assertSafeArg` (include_files doesn't bypass it), the hash-shaped-commit-subject edge case, a real multi-line commit body still parses correctly (proving the separate-numstat-call design choice), a 15-file commit reports all 15 files with correct total additions, 10 concurrent calls consistent, JSON-serialisability. - [x] Proactive: add a `git_blame`-derived `git_ownership` tool — aggregate blame lines by author for a file or directory tree ("who owns this code") — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session. Verified full suite (1212/1212 passing) and clean git status before starting. Picked direction (2) from the two options the previous session left (code-ownership tool over the "disk audit" wrapper, since the audit direction is trivially buildable by the caller via execute_pipeline already and wouldn't earn its keep as a distinct tool). New lib/gitOwnershipOps.js: `blameAuthorCounts(filePath, repoRoot)` uses `git blame --porcelain` (NOT --line-porcelain — porcelain only repeats the full header block on a hash's first occurrence, so a hash-to-author map plus a running currentHash across tab-prefixed content lines is enough to attribute every line without paying for repeated headers/content on every line). `gitOwnership(absTarget, clientPath, isDirectory, jailBoundary, opts)`: for a directory, enumerates tracked files via `git ls-files -- <path>` (respects .gitignore) capped at `max_files` (clamped 1-500, default 100, `truncated: true` beyond the cap); for a single file, blames just that file. Returns `{ path, filesScanned, filesSkipped, truncated, totalLines, authors: [{name, lines, percentage}] }` sorted lines-descending. Reuses existing gitExec/assertSafeArg/q from lib/gitOpsHelpers.js — no new shell-safety surface for the git commands themselves.

    **Two real bugs found and fixed during isolated testing (Tester role), one of them a genuine security issue:**
    1. **Jail-escape via unbounded repo-root discovery (security).** The first implementation had the caller (dispatchRead.js) pass a `repoDir` and let git's own upward `.git` discovery + the existing `GIT_CEILING_DIRECTORIES = dirname(cwd)` convention (used by every other git_* tool) find the repo root. That convention only works when cwd is already the repo root; here the tool intentionally lets callers point at an arbitrary subdirectory, and when that subdirectory's immediate parent is exactly where `.git` lives, the ceiling forbids git from ever entering that parent, so discovery silently fails — reproduced with a real test (`own-empty/untracked-sub` inside a fresh test repo). Rewrote repo-root discovery to walk upward from the target using `fs.existsSync(path.join(dir, ".git"))` ourselves (`findRepoRoot`), with all subsequent git commands run with that discovered root as cwd. **This surfaced a second, more serious problem**: with no boundary, the walk-up doesn't stop at the sandbox — on this machine a non-git test directory under the OS temp folder walked all the way up to `C:\Users\<user>` and silently adopted an unrelated `.git` (e.g. a dotfiles repo) found there, meaning `git ls-files`/`git blame` would have run with a cwd *outside the jailed MCP root entirely* — a real sandbox-escape vector (read access to an arbitrary ancestor repo on the host, not just an internal bug). Fixed by threading the jailed root (`resolveClientPath`'s `root` field, the same boundary every other tool trusts) through as a mandatory `jailBoundary` argument that `findRepoRoot` never ascends past, regardless of whether `.git` is found there or not. Added a dedicated regression test (`git_ownership: repo-root discovery never ascends above the jailed MCP root`) asserting a non-git directory inside the sandbox always throws "not inside a git repository" rather than silently borrowing an ancestor repo from outside it.
    2. **Single-file vs. directory-mode error semantics (test-design bug caught by a failing test, then a real behavior gap fixed).** The original code caught blame failures uniformly (both modes) and recorded them in `filesSkipped`, so requesting ownership of one explicitly-named untracked/unblameable file silently returned an empty, successful-looking result instead of an error — misleading for a single-file call where the caller named exactly that file. Directory-mode scans still correctly skip-and-continue past individual unblameable files (a binary file, etc.) without aborting the whole tree scan; single-file mode now lets the blame failure propagate directly as the whole answer.

    Also fixed a test-authoring bug of my own during the same pass: a multi-author stress test asserted exactly 5 distinct authors across 20 added files, forgetting the fixture repo's own initial `readme.txt` commit (authored as "Test User" by the shared `makeRepo` helper) is itself a 6th tracked file/author in the aggregate — corrected the assertion to expect 6 authors and exclude "Test User" from the per-author line-count check.

    Wiring: lib/dispatchRead.js `git_ownership` handler (passes `resolveClientPath`'s `root` through as the jail boundary), lib/schemas/gitSchemas.js schema (required `path`, optional `max_files`/`extensions`), lib/schemas/execSchemas.js execute_pipeline enum. New test/sections/41-git-ownership.js — 24 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme (single-file and directory-mode happy path, percentage math, sort order, result field shape, missing-path -32602, empty/untracked-only directory, max_files clamping/truncation, extensions filter, non-git-directory error, **jail-boundary escape regression**, untracked single-file throws, binary file in directory mode skipped via filesSkipped without aborting the scan, path traversal + absolute-path-outside-root blocked, injection-shaped file content and author name round-trip literally, JSON-serialisability, no prototype pollution, 5-author/20-file stress aggregate, wide-tree truncation, 10 concurrent calls consistent, non-numeric max_files fuzz falls back to default, cleanup). Wired into test/run-tests.js as section [44]. Full suite: **1236 passed, 0 failed** (1212 prior + 24 new). Cleaned 7 stray `.bak` files generated by this session's own `replace_in_file`/`write_file` calls (dispatchRead.js.bak, gitOwnershipOps.js.bak, schemas/execSchemas.js.bak, schemas/gitSchemas.js.bak, README.md.bak, run-tests.js.bak, sections/41-git-ownership.js.bak) plus the temporary test_output_verify.txt/test_output_full.txt logs. README updated: version v3.23.0 → v3.24.0, new `git_ownership` bullet added under Git Metadata Tools ("eight"→"nine" never-require-exec sentence), new `lib/gitOwnershipOps.js` Code Layout row added. All lib/ and test/ files remain under the 500-line threshold (largest touched file: test/sections/41-git-ownership.js at 350 lines).

- [x] Proactive: audit the other pre-existing git_* tools (git_status, git_log, git_blame, git_diff, git_stash_list, git_branch_list, git_show, git_tag_list) for the same "cwd is a subdirectory, not the repo root" gap that git_ownership had — status: tested
  - notes: Completed this session (previous session had extracted `findRepoRoot` out of lib/gitOwnershipOps.js into the shared lib/gitOpsHelpers.js — with a doc comment already claiming "every other git_* tool's dispatch handler uses it too" — but had NOT actually wired any of the other 8 tools to use it yet; only lib/gitOwnershipOps.js itself imported it, verified via `grep -n findRepoRoot` across every git_*Ops.js file. task.md and the two touched lib/ files were left uncommitted from that cutoff). Confirmed the audited gap for the remaining tools: every git_* dispatch handler in lib/dispatchRead.js resolved `repoDir` via a plain `resolveClientPath(args.path).resolved` (or the first configured MCP root when `path` was omitted) and handed that straight to `gitExec()`, which relies on git's own upward `.git`-discovery bounded by `GIT_CEILING_DIRECTORIES=dirname(cwd)`. That ceiling sits exactly one level above cwd, so it does not actually let git climb *any* levels above the immediate target directory before stopping — a `path` nested two or more levels inside a real repo (with no `.git` in its immediate parent) silently failed with "not a git repository" even though it plainly is one. (This is a functional correctness gap for these 8 tools, not itself a jail-escape — the ceiling variable already prevented runaway upward climbing; the jail-escape variant was specific to `git_ownership`'s custom, unbounded discovery loop before its own earlier fix.)

    Fix: added a new `resolveRepoDir(argPath)` helper in lib/dispatchRead.js that calls `resolveClientPath()` then `findRepoRoot(resolved, root)` (the same shared, jail-bounded helper `git_ownership` uses), falling back to the originally-resolved directory when no `.git` is found anywhere between the target and the jail boundary — so genuinely non-git paths still surface the same "not a git repository" error as before, only genuinely-nested-but-real repos are fixed. Wired into all 8 remaining dispatch handlers: `git_status`, `git_log`, `git_diff`, `git_stash_list`, `git_branch_list`, `git_show`, `git_tag_list` now call `resolveRepoDir(args.path)`; `git_blame` (which resolves a *file*, not a directory) calls `findRepoRoot(path.dirname(resolved), root)` directly since its repo-root search has to start from the file's containing directory rather than the file itself. `lib/gitOwnershipOps.js`'s own doc comment referencing "every other git_* tool's dispatch handler uses it too" is now actually accurate.

    New test/sections/42-git-nested-repo-root.js — 16 tests across Normal/Medium/High/Critical/Extreme: each of the 8 tools succeeds (rather than throwing) when called with a path 2-3 levels deep inside a real repo and returns data consistent with calling the same tool at the repo root directly (git_status branch/clean, git_log commit count+hash, git_blame line count, git_diff stat_only changedFiles, git_stash_list message, git_branch_list sees a branch created off the nested repo, git_show reads file content at HEAD, git_tag_list sees a tag); a 1-level-deep subdirectory (the previously-already-tolerated case) still works unchanged; omitting `path` entirely is unaffected; a repo nested 5 levels deep still resolves; the jail-boundary regression is re-verified per-tool (a non-git directory inside the sandbox — including a 3-level-deep non-git nested path — always throws "not a git repository", never silently adopts an unrelated ancestor repo from outside the jail, mirroring `git_ownership`'s own jail-escape regression test); 10 concurrent nested-path `git_status` calls return consistent results. One test-authoring bug caught and fixed during my own verification pass (not an implementation bug): the `git_show` test initially passed a bare `file: "deep.txt"` — but `git_show`'s `file` argument is always relative to the *repo root* (unchanged by this fix, which only changes *which directory `git` runs in*, not how `file` paths are interpreted), so it needed the full repo-root-relative path (`lvl1/lvl2/deep.txt`) instead. Wired into test/run-tests.js as section [45]. Full suite re-run twice after the fix: **1252 passed, 0 failed** both times (1236 prior + 16 new). Cleaned 6 stray `.bak` files left over from the previous session's cutoff plus this session's own `replace_in_file` calls (`.gitignore.bak`, `task.md.bak`, `lib/dispatchRead.js.bak`, `lib/gitOpsHelpers.js.bak`, `lib/gitOwnershipOps.js.bak`, `test/run-tests.js.bak`, `test/sections/42-git-nested-repo-root.js.bak`) plus 5 stray `test_output_*.txt` logs (already gitignored). README updated: version v3.24.0 → v3.25.0, new paragraph under the Git Metadata Tools section documenting that all nine tools now share the jail-bounded `findRepoRoot` repo-root discovery. All lib/ and test/ files remain under the 500-line threshold (lib/dispatchRead.js 373 lines, test/sections/42-git-nested-repo-root.js 231 lines).
